<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p><b>Matthew Joseph "Matt" Korklan</b> (born March 19, 1983), also known by the <a href="/wiki/Ring_name" title="Ring name">ring name</a> <b>Matt Sydal</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestler</a>, perhaps best known for his time in <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a> under the ring name <b>Evan Bourne</b>.</p>
<p>Between 2000 and 2007, Korklan wrestled on the independent circuit, for <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_promotion" title="Professional wrestling promotion">promotions</a> including <a href="/wiki/National_Wrestling_Alliance" title="National Wrestling Alliance">NWA Midwest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Independent_Wrestling_Association_Mid-South" title="Independent Wrestling Association Mid-South">IWA-Mid South</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Honor" title="Ring of Honor">Ring of Honor</a>, winning both singles and tag team championships. He also wrestled for the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_Society_X" title="Wrestling Society X">Wrestling Society X</a> and was featured on <a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling" title="Total Nonstop Action Wrestling">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling</a>'s early <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-view" title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a> events. Beginning in 2005, he wrestled for <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Gate" title="Dragon Gate">Dragon Gate</a> in Japan, and won the <a href="/wiki/Open_the_Brave_Gate_Championship" title="Open the Brave Gate Championship">Open the Brave Gate Championship</a> in early 2007. Korklan signed with WWE in 2007, and made his main roster debut as Evan Bourne on <a href="/wiki/ECW_(WWE)" title="ECW (WWE)">ECW</a> the following year. In 2011, he formed an alliance with <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Kingston" title="Kofi Kingston">Kofi Kingston</a>, known as Air Boom, and they won the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WWE Raw Tag Team Championship">WWE Tag Team Championship</a>. In 2012, Korklan was suspended for violating WWE's wellness policy, and then suffered foot injuries in a motorcycle accident, forcing him out of action. Without reappearing on television, he was released from WWE in 2014 and returned to wrestling on the independent circuit under his former ring name. He also made his debut for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Japan_Pro_Wrestling" title="New Japan Pro Wrestling">New Japan Pro Wrestling</a> (NJPW), where he is a former two-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IWGP_Junior_Heavyweight_Tag_Team_Champion" title="IWGP Junior Heavyweight Tag Team Champion">IWGP Junior Heavyweight Tag Team Champion</a> and a one-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NEVER_Openweight_6-Man_Tag_Team_Champion" title="NEVER Openweight 6-Man Tag Team Champion">NEVER Openweight 6-Man Tag Team Champion</a>.</p>
<p>He is known for his high flying, <a href="/wiki/Lucha_libre" title="Lucha libre">lucha libre</a>-inspired style of wrestling, and was named the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrestling_Observer_Newsletter" title="Wrestling Observer Newsletter">Wrestling Observer Newsletter</a></i>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Flying_Wrestler" title="Best Flying Wrestler">Best Flying Wrestler</a> in 2008.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_wrestling_career">Professional wrestling career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Professional wrestling career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_and_independent_circuit_.282000.E2.80.932007.29">Training and independent circuit (2000–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Training and independent circuit (2000–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Korklan was on his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high school</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_wrestling" title="Sport wrestling">wrestling</a> team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-slam-1">[1]</a></sup> While a senior in high school, Korklan began training with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis, Missouri</a>-based Gateway Championship Wrestling (GCW) promotion. After three months of training, Korklan began wrestling for GCW on October 20, 2000, becoming the first person under the age of 18 to receive a wrestler's license in Missouri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-slam-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWOW_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-OWOW-4">[4]</a></sup> Prior to this, Korklan had briefly wrestled as Lance Sydal in the <a href="/wiki/Backyard_wrestling" title="Backyard wrestling">backyard wrestling</a> promotion, Saint Peters Wrestling Organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-slam-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, Korklan (now known as Matt, forgoing a surname)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWOW_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-OWOW-4">[4]</a></sup> formed a <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Stable" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">stable</a> in GCW, known as Operation:Shamrock. In addition, Korklan and fellow stable member Billy McNeil formed a <a href="/wiki/Tag_team" title="Tag team">tag team</a>. Operation: Shamrock maintained a <a href="/wiki/Feud_(professional_wrestling)" title="Feud (professional wrestling)">feud</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Heel_(professional_wrestling)" title="Heel (professional wrestling)">villainous</a> Ministry of Hate faction, led by Nikki Strychnine.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg/220px-Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg/330px-Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg/440px-Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matt_Sydal_at_a_Chikara_show.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sydal at a <a href="/wiki/Chikara_(professional_wrestling)" title="Chikara (professional wrestling)">Chikara</a> show in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Korklan debuted in <a href="/wiki/Independent_Wrestling_Association_Mid-South" title="Independent Wrestling Association Mid-South">Independent Wrestling Association Mid-South</a> (IWA Mid-South) in November 2003, combining two of his old ring names into a new one, Matt Sydal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-slam-1">[1]</a></sup> He won his first championship, the <a href="/wiki/IWA_Mid-South_Light_Heavyweight_Championship" title="IWA Mid-South Light Heavyweight Championship">IWA Mid-South Light Heavyweight Championship</a>, on January 17, 2004, by defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.C._Bailey" title="J.C. Bailey">J.C. Bailey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IWA_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-IWA-5">[5]</a></sup> Sydal lost the title to <a href="/wiki/Delirious_(wrestler)" title="Delirious (wrestler)">Delirious</a> on June 26, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IWA_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-IWA-5">[5]</a></sup> Sydal joined <a href="/wiki/National_Wrestling_Alliance" title="National Wrestling Alliance">NWA Midwest</a> that same year. On July 30, he defeated Justin Kage for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NWA_Midwest_X_Division_Championship" title="NWA Midwest X Division Championship">NWA Midwest X Division Championship</a>, which he lost to Delirious after holding it for nearly a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-X_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-X-6">[6]</a></sup> Sydal teamed with <a href="/wiki/Daizee_Haze" title="Daizee Haze">Daizee Haze</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Intergender_wrestling" title="Intergender wrestling">intergender</a> <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_tag_team_match_types" title="Professional wrestling tag team match types">tag team match</a> against Delirious and <a href="/wiki/MsChif" title="MsChif">MsChif</a>, of which the male wrestler on the winning team would become champion. Haze pinned MsChif to win the title for Sydal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-X_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-X-6">[6]</a></sup> Sydal lost the title to Jaysin Strife roughly four months later<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-X_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-X-6">[6]</a></sup> before leaving the promotion.</p>
<p>Sydal wrestled several top independent stars during his time as a regular in IWA. He lost three matches to <a href="/wiki/A.J._Styles" title="A.J. Styles">A.J. Styles</a> during a short-lived feud. He also faced <a href="/wiki/CM_Punk" title="CM Punk">CM Punk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Sabin" title="Chris Sabin">Chris Sabin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nate_Webb" title="Nate Webb">Nate Webb</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWOW_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-OWOW-4">[4]</a></sup> On September 24, 2005, Sydal won the fifth <a href="/wiki/Ted_Petty_Invitational" title="Ted Petty Invitational">Ted Petty Invitational</a> tournament, defeating <a href="/wiki/Sami_Zayn" title="Sami Zayn">El Generico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seth_Rollins" title="Seth Rollins">Tyler Black</a>, and Sabin to reach the final match, where he defeated <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Owens" title="Kevin Owens">Kevin Steen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arik_Cannon" title="Arik Cannon">Arik Cannon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ted_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ted-7">[7]</a></sup> Afterwards, Sydal appeared infrequently in IWA, lastly in August 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWOW_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-OWOW-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling_.282004.E2.80.932005.29">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling (2004–2005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Total Nonstop Action Wrestling (2004–2005)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sydal wrestled on <a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling" title="Total Nonstop Action Wrestling">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling</a> (TNA)'s first monthly pay-per-view event, <a href="/wiki/Victory_Road_(2004)" title="Victory Road (2004)">Victory Road</a>. He participated in a twenty-man <a href="/wiki/X_Division" title="X Division">X Division</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauntlet_for_the_Gold" title="Gauntlet for the Gold">Gauntlet for the Gold</a> match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Sydal was a candidate in an online poll to determine who would meet <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Daniels" title="Christopher Daniels">Christopher Daniels</a> for the <a href="/wiki/TNA_X_Division_Championship" title="TNA X Division Championship">TNA X Division Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sacrifice_(2005)" title="Sacrifice (2005)">Sacrifice</a>, but was not chosen. During his run in TNA, Sydal was used as a <a href="/wiki/Job_(professional_wrestling)" title="Job (professional wrestling)">jobber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWOW_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-OWOW-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ring_of_Honor_.282004.E2.80.932007.29">Ring of Honor (2004–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ring of Honor (2004–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AJ_%26_Matt....jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="830" data-file-width="795" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/AJ_%26_Matt....jpg/220px-AJ_%26_Matt....jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/AJ_%26_Matt....jpg/330px-AJ_%26_Matt....jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/AJ_%26_Matt....jpg/440px-AJ_%26_Matt....jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AJ_%26_Matt....jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sydal with <a href="/wiki/A.J._Styles" title="A.J. Styles">A.J. Styles</a> (left) in Ring of Honor during 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sydal (along with his valet, Daizee Haze) debuted in <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Honor" title="Ring of Honor">Ring of Honor</a> at <i>Reborn: Stage One</i> on April 23, 2004, defeating his nemesis, Delirious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROHresults_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ROHresults-9">[9]</a></sup> Following a brief feud with <a href="/wiki/Trent_Acid" title="Trent Acid">Trent Acid</a>, Sydal teamed with Fast Eddie Vegas as The Air Devils, a name chosen by ROH fans. They only teamed once, on February 25, 2005, at <i>3rd Anniversary: Part 2</i>, defeating <a href="/wiki/The_Ring_Crew_Express" title="The Ring Crew Express">The Ring Crew Express</a>. After the match, Vegas <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turned_heel" title="Turned heel">turned</a> on Sydal and joined the <a href="/wiki/Heel_(professional_wrestling)" title="Heel (professional wrestling)">heel</a> stable, <a href="/wiki/The_Embassy_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Embassy (professional wrestling)">The Embassy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWOW_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-OWOW-4">[4]</a></sup> On August 12, Sydal and Haze joined Austin Aries, <a href="/wiki/Roderick_Strong" title="Roderick Strong">Roderick Strong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Evans_(wrestler)" title="Jack Evans (wrestler)">Jack Evans</a> in <a href="/wiki/Generation_Next" title="Generation Next">Generation Next</a>, a stable in the midst of a feud with The Embassy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rajah_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rajah-10">[10]</a></sup> In late 2005, Haze turned on Sydal, leaving him and Generation Next and joining The Embassy. Generation Next fought The Embassy in several multi-man tag matches, culminating in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steel_Cage_match" title="Steel Cage match">Steel Cage Warfare</a> match on December 3, which Generation Next won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROHresults_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-ROHresults-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>After wrestling A.J. Styles at <i>Hell Freezes Over</i>, the two teamed to unsuccessfully challenge Sydal's Generation Next stablemates, Austin Aries and Roderick Strong, for the <a href="/wiki/ROH_World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="ROH World Tag Team Championship">ROH World Tag Team Championship</a>. Sydal also teamed with <a href="/wiki/Samoa_Joe" title="Samoa Joe">Samoa Joe</a> and Jack Evans to chase the title. Sydal went to the finals of the <a href="/wiki/ROH_Survival_of_the_Fittest#Survival_of_the_Fittest_2006" title="ROH Survival of the Fittest">2006 Survival of the Fittest tournament</a>, before losing to Delirious. Sydal and Delirious renewed their rivalry in ROH, wrestling several matches in mid-2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROHresults_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-ROHresults-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>After several matches against each other in 2006, Sydal teamed with Christopher Daniels in another attempt to win the ROH World Tag Team Championship. They feuded with the champions, <a href="/wiki/The_Kings_of_Wrestling" title="The Kings of Wrestling">The Kings of Wrestling</a>, before winning the championship at <i>Dethroned</i>. Sydal and Daniels successfully defended the title against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobuhiko_Oshima" title="Nobuhiko Oshima">CIMA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shingo_Takagi" title="Shingo Takagi">Shingo</a>, and former champions Austin Aries and Roderick Strong, before losing it to <a href="/wiki/The_Briscoe_Brothers" title="The Briscoe Brothers">The Briscoe Brothers</a> at the <i>Fifth Year Festival: Chicago</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROHtag_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-ROHtag-11">[11]</a></sup> During their title reign, Sydal developed a <a href="/wiki/Self-confidence" title="Self-confidence">cocky</a>, heelish attitude. After unsuccessful attempts (with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antonio_Cesaro" title="Antonio Cesaro">Claudio Castagnoli</a>) to regain the title, Sydal joined <a href="/wiki/Larry_Sweeney" title="Larry Sweeney">Larry Sweeney's</a> heel stable Sweet n' Sour Inc. (which also included Chris Hero, <a href="/wiki/Sara_Del_Rey" title="Sara Del Rey">Sara Del Rey</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Toland_(wrestler)" title="John Toland (wrestler)">Tank Toland</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sweeney_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sweeney-12">[12]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/ROH_Man_Up" title="ROH Man Up">Man Up</a>, Sydal wrestled his final match for ROH, losing to long-time rival Delirious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROHresults_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-ROHresults-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dragon_Gate_and_Wrestling_Society_X_.282006.E2.80.932007.29">Dragon Gate and Wrestling Society X (2006–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Dragon Gate and Wrestling Society X (2006–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sydal began touring Japan with <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Gate" title="Dragon Gate">Dragon Gate</a> in May 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MayDGresults_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-MayDGresults-13">[13]</a></sup> There, he aligned with CIMA, Don Fuji, and Jack Evans to form the stable New Blood Generation International. He also became a part of CIMA's Typhoon stable. At Wrestlejam, Sydal teamed with Generation Next stablemate Roderick Strong to win the $10,000 Tag Team Challenge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MayDGresults_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-MayDGresults-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 12, 2007, Sydal won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_Gate_Open_the_Brave_Gate_Championship" title="Dragon Gate Open the Brave Gate Championship">Dragon Gate Open the Brave Gate Championship</a> from <a href="/wiki/Masato_Yoshino" title="Masato Yoshino">Masato Yoshino</a>, becoming the first <a href="/wiki/Gaijin" title="Gaijin">gaijin</a> to hold the championship. He held it for just over a month, successfully defending it against Yoshino in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyogo" title="Hyogo">Hyogo</a> and against <a href="/wiki/Austin_Aries" title="Austin Aries">Austin Aries</a> at Ring of Honor's <i>Fifth Year Festival: Dayton</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROHresults_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-ROHresults-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BraveGate_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-BraveGate-14">[14]</a></sup> He dropped the title to <a href="/wiki/Genki_Horiguchi" title="Genki Horiguchi">Genki Horiguchi</a> on March 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DG2007results_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-DG2007results-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DG_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-DG-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sydal was a part of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> promotion, <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_Society_X" title="Wrestling Society X">Wrestling Society X</a>, where he competed as a <a href="/wiki/Heel_(professional_wrestling)" title="Heel (professional wrestling)">heel</a> against Jack Evans, <a href="/wiki/Scorpio_Sky" title="Scorpio Sky">Scorpio Sky</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Human_Tornado" title="Human Tornado">Human Tornado</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSX_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSX-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> He began a feud with <a href="/wiki/Sean_Waltman" title="Sean Waltman">Syxx-Pac</a> over Sydal's <a href="/wiki/Manager_(professional_wrestling)#Managers_vs._valets_vs._enforcers" title="Manager (professional wrestling)">valet</a> and on-screen girlfriend <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Miklosi" title="Elizabeth Miklosi">Lizzy Valentine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSX_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-WSX-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-20">[20]</a></sup> but WSX folded before they ever had a match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSX_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-WSX-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wrestling_Entertainment_.2F_WWE">World Wrestling Entertainment / WWE</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: World Wrestling Entertainment / WWE">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ohio_Valley_Wrestling_.282007.E2.80.932008.29">Ohio Valley Wrestling (2007–2008)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ohio Valley Wrestling (2007–2008)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following the expiration of his WSX contract and the close of the promotion, Korklan signed a developmental contract with World Wrestling Entertainment (WWE).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Sydal debuted in <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Valley_Wrestling" title="Ohio Valley Wrestling">Ohio Valley Wrestling</a> (OVW) at its October 10, 2007 TV taping, defeating <a href="/wiki/Jamin_Olivencia" title="Jamin Olivencia">Jamin Olivencia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In December, Sydal defeated <a href="/wiki/Mike_Kruel" title="Mike Kruel">Mike Kruel</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/OVW_Heavyweight_Championship" title="OVW Heavyweight Championship">OVW Heavyweight Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OVW_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-OVW-24">[24]</a></sup> On February 7, 2008 WWE announced it had ended its affiliation with OVW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> As a result, Sydal lost the OVW Heavyweight Championship to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brad_Bradley" title="Brad Bradley">Jay Bradley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OVW_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-OVW-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_Championship_Wrestling_.282008.29">Florida Championship Wrestling (2008)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Florida Championship Wrestling (2008)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sydal joined WWE's new developmental territory <a href="/wiki/Florida_Championship_Wrestling" title="Florida Championship Wrestling">Florida Championship Wrestling</a>, debuting on March 22, 2008, and defeating <a href="/wiki/Tyson_Kidd" title="Tyson Kidd">TJ Wilson</a>. He was then called up to WWE's main roster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-slam-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_switches_.282008.E2.80.932011.29">Brand switches (2008–2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Brand switches (2008–2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sydal made his debut for the <a href="/wiki/ECW_(WWE)" title="ECW (WWE)">ECW</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_Brand_Extension" title="WWE Brand Extension">brand</a> on June 3, 2008, as a <a href="/wiki/Face_(professional_wrestling)" title="Face (professional wrestling)">face</a> character. He lost a match by <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling#Countout" title="Professional wrestling">countout</a> to <a href="/wiki/Shelton_Benjamin" title="Shelton Benjamin">Shelton Benjamin</a>, after he was thrown at guest commentator <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Kingston" title="Kofi Kingston">Kofi Kingston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The following week on <i>ECW</i>, he (now renamed Evan Bourne) teamed with Kofi Kingston to defeat Benjamin and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Knox" title="Mike Knox">Mike Knox</a> in a tag team match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In the following weeks, Bourne defeated <a href="/wiki/Matt_Striker" title="Matt Striker">Matt Striker</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Maritato" title="James Maritato">Nunzio</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chavo_Guerrero,_Jr." title="Chavo Guerrero, Jr.">Chavo Guerrero</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> using the <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_aerial_techniques#Shooting_star_press" title="Professional wrestling aerial techniques">shooting star press</a> as his <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Finisher" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">finishing maneuver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWEbio_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-WWEbio-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evan_Bourne_.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="961" data-file-width="390" height="542" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Evan_Bourne_.jpg/220px-Evan_Bourne_.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Evan_Bourne_.jpg/330px-Evan_Bourne_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/53/Evan_Bourne_.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evan_Bourne_.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bourne making his ring entrance on an episode of <i>ECW</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bourne also appeared on the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a> brand, saving <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ey_Mysterio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ey Mysterio (page does not exist)">ey Mysterio</a> from an assault by <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Kane</a>. The two defeated <a href="/wiki/John_Morrison_and_The_Miz" title="John Morrison and The Miz">John Morrison and The Miz</a> the following week. At <a href="/wiki/Cyber_Sunday_(2008)" title="Cyber Sunday (2008)">Cyber Sunday</a> in October, WWE fans chose Bourne to face <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt Hardy</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECW_Championship" title="ECW Championship">ECW Championship</a>. He was pinned after Hardy performed a <a href="/wiki/Cutter_(professional_wrestling)#Twist_of_Fate" title="Cutter (professional wrestling)">Twist of Fate</a> on him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Two days later, during a six-man tag match on <i>ECW</i>, he landed a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_aerial_techniques" title="Professional wrestling aerial techniques">dive from the ring</a> on his right ankle, dislocating it and tearing his deltoid ligament. Surgery was not necessary, but Bourne was not medically cleared to return to the ring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> On December 8, he won the "Best Finishing Maneuver" Slammy award for his shooting star press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slammy_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slammy-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the March 10, 2009, episode of <i>ECW</i>, a vignette aired, promoting Bourne's return on March 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In his return match, he defeated <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Noble" title="Jamie Noble">Jamie Noble</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 29, Bourne was traded to the Raw brand, and made his debut that night as the first of three wrestlers in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Gauntlet_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">Gauntlet match</a> against <a href="/wiki/WWE_Championship" title="WWE Championship">WWE Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Randy_Orton" title="Randy Orton">Randy Orton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> On the November 2 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a></i>, he lost a United States Championship match to The Miz. On the December 29 episode of <i>ECW</i>, he defeated Mike Knox in an "ECW Homecoming" match to qualify for the "Homecoming Battle Royal", which would decide the opponent for ECW Champion <a href="/wiki/Christian_Cage" title="Christian Cage">Christian</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2010)" title="Royal Rumble (2010)">Royal Rumble</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bourne lost a non-title match to WWE Champion <a href="/wiki/Sheamus" title="Sheamus">Sheamus</a> on the January 4, 2010, episode of <i>Raw</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The following week on <i>ECW</i>, he competed in the "Homecoming Battle Royal" but was the first man eliminated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> On the March 8 episode of <i>Raw</i>, he defeated <a href="/wiki/William_Regal" title="William Regal">William Regal</a> to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/Money_in_the_Bank_ladder_match" title="Money in the Bank ladder match">Money in the Bank ladder match</a> at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXVI" title="WrestleMania XXVI">WrestleMania XXVI</a>, which was won by <a href="/wiki/Jack_Swagger" title="Jack Swagger">Jack Swagger</a>.</p>
<p>The May 31, 2010 episode of <i>Raw</i> opened with Bourne being assaulted by <a href="/wiki/Edge_(wrestler)" title="Edge (wrestler)">Edge</a>, after Bourne proposed Edge put his spot in the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Championship" title="WWE Championship">WWE Championship</a> match at <a href="/wiki/WWE_Fatal_4-Way" title="WWE Fatal 4-Way">Fatal 4-Way</a> on the line in a match. Later in the show, <a href="/wiki/John_Cena" title="John Cena">John Cena</a> chose Bourne to replace his scheduled tag team partner, Randy Orton (who was earlier "injured" by Edge), in a match against Edge and Sheamus. Bourne pinned Sheamus to earn the victory for his team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Two weeks later, Bourne defeated <a href="/wiki/Chris_Jericho" title="Chris Jericho">Chris Jericho</a> by disqualification. Jericho had threatened the referee and attacked Bourne while he was in the ropes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> At Fatal 4-Way, he pinned Jericho in a rematch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The following night on <i>Raw</i>, Jericho challenged Bourne to a third match, stating he would leave WWE if he lost; Jericho pinned Bourne to win the match and stay with the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> On the July 5 <i>Raw</i>, Bourne teamed with Randy Orton to defeat Jericho and Edge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Bourne competed in the <a href="/wiki/Money_in_the_Bank_ladder_match" title="Money in the Bank ladder match">Money in the Bank ladder match</a> at <a href="/wiki/Money_in_the_Bank_(2010)" title="Money in the Bank (2010)">Money in the Bank</a> on July 18, but lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 19, at <a href="/wiki/Night_of_Champions_(2010)" title="Night of Champions (2010)">Night of Champions</a>, Bourne teamed with Mark Henry in the Tag Team Turmoil match for the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WWE Raw Tag Team Championship">WWE Tag Team Championship</a>. They were the final team eliminated, by <a href="/wiki/Drew_Galloway" title="Drew Galloway">Drew McIntyre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cody_Rhodes" title="Cody Rhodes">Cody Rhodes</a>. On the October 11 <i>Raw</i>, he lost a match (to decide who would be on Team Raw at <a href="/wiki/Bragging_Rights_(2010)" title="Bragging Rights (2010)">Bragging Rights</a>) to <a href="/wiki/CM_Punk" title="CM Punk">CM Punk</a>, and was subsequently assaulted. This assault was the storyline reason to remove Bourne from television. In reality, he had shoulder surgery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bourne returned on the February 28, 2011 episode of <i>Raw</i>, defeating Sheamus after Sheamus was attacked by <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Triple H</a> before the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> On May 23, he began feuding with Jack Swagger, with the two trading victories on several episodes of <i>Raw</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Bourne then defeated Swagger at <a href="/wiki/WWE_Capitol_Punishment" title="WWE Capitol Punishment">WWE Capitol Punishment</a> to end the feud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tag_Team_Champion_and_injury_.282011.E2.80.932014.29">Tag Team Champion and injury (2011–2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tag Team Champion and injury (2011–2014)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1013" data-file-width="914" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg/220px-Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg/330px-Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg/440px-Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bourne-Tag-Champ-2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bourne with the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WWE Raw Tag Team Championship">WWE Tag Team Championship</a> belt in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the August 22, 2011, episode of <i>Raw</i>, Bourne won his first championship in WWE. He and <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Kingston" title="Kofi Kingston">Kofi Kingston</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/David_Otunga" title="David Otunga">David Otunga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Axel" title="Curtis Axel">Michael McGillicutty</a> for the WWE Tag Team Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> On the August 29 <i>Raw</i>, the team was named Air Boom and made their first title defense, defeating Otunga and McGillicutty in a rematch. At <a href="/wiki/Night_of_Champions_(2011)" title="Night of Champions (2011)">Night of Champions</a>, Air Boom retained the title against The Miz and R-Truth when The Miz was disqualified for attacking the referee. At both <a href="/wiki/Hell_in_a_Cell_(2011)" title="Hell in a Cell (2011)">Hell in a Cell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vengeance_(2011)" title="Vengeance (2011)">Vengeance</a>, Air Boom retained the title against <a href="/wiki/Dolph_Ziggler" title="Dolph Ziggler">Dolph Ziggler</a> and Jack Swagger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 1, WWE announced it had suspended Korklan for 30 days for his first violation of the company’s wellness policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Bourne returned to television on December 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> On December 18, at <a href="/wiki/TLC:_Tables,_Ladders_%26_Chairs_(2011)" title="TLC: Tables, Ladders &amp; Chairs (2011)">Tables, Ladders &amp; Chairs</a>, Air Boom retained the Tag Team Championship by defeating <a href="/wiki/Primo_%26_Epico" title="Primo &amp; Epico">Primo &amp; Epico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> On January 15, 2012, Air Boom lost the WWE Tag Team Championship to Primo and Epico at a house show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The following night on <i>Raw</i>, Air Boom was awarded a rematch, but failed to regain the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The following day on January 17, Korklan was suspended for 60 days for his second failure of a wellness test.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2012, Korklan was involved in a car accident which broke his foot in four places and dislocated it in five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> After a year-long absence, Bourne returned on March 28, 2013, at a <a href="/wiki/WWE_NXT" title="WWE NXT">NXT</a> live event, defeating <a href="/wiki/Sami_Zayn" title="Sami Zayn">Sami Zayn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The following year, on June 12, WWE announced that Korklan had been released from his contract, without him reappearing on television.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_the_independent_circuit_.282014.E2.80.932015.29">Return to the independent circuit (2014–2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Return to the independent circuit (2014–2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From August 30 to 31, Sydal took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Los_Angeles_(professional_wrestling)#2014" title="Battle of Los Angeles (professional wrestling)">2014's Battle of Los Angeles</a>. After winning against Chris Hero, he was later eliminated from the tournament by <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Omega" title="Kenny Omega">Kenny Omega</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On February 7, 2015, Sydal debuted For <a href="/wiki/Family_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="Family Wrestling Entertainment">Family Wrestling Entertainment</a> (FWE), unsuccessfully challenging <a href="/wiki/Paul_London" title="Paul London">Paul London</a> for the FWE Tri-Borough Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> On December 11, Sydal unsuccessfully challenged Roderick Strong for the PWG World Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sydal became active in the UK scene, most notably in <a href="/wiki/Revolution_Pro_Wrestling" title="Revolution Pro Wrestling">Revolution Pro Wrestling</a>, feuding with <a href="/wiki/Will_Ospreay" title="Will Ospreay">Will Ospreay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 3, 2015, at a show in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, Sydal briefly held the PWF Lord of the World Championship, defeating Namsuk Kim, before being defeated in an immediate rematch. This was his first singles championship since leaving WWE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolve_.282014.29">Evolve (2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Evolve (2014)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 8, Sydal made his debut for <a href="/wiki/Evolve_(professional_wrestling)" title="Evolve (professional wrestling)">Evolve</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Gargano" title="Johnny Gargano">Johnny Gargano</a>. The following night, Sydal unsuccessfully challenged <a href="/wiki/Ricochet_(wrestler)" title="Ricochet (wrestler)">Ricochet</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Open_the_Freedom_Gate_Championship" title="Open the Freedom Gate Championship">Open the Freedom Gate Championship</a> in the main-event of EVOLVE 32.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_DG_.282014.E2.80.932015.29">Return to DG (2014–2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Return to DG (2014–2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On July 20, 2014, he made his in-ring return to Dragon Gate, tagging with Cima to take on Ricochet and <a href="/wiki/Masato_Yoshino" title="Masato Yoshino">Masato Yoshino</a>. They came up short in the bout, when Cima tapped out to Yoshino.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> After another year away from Dragon Gate, Sydal made a surprise return to the promotion on June 28, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On July 20, Sydal and Ricochet unsuccessfully challenged <a href="/wiki/Naruki_Doi" title="Naruki Doi">Naruki Doi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yamato_(wrestler)" title="Yamato (wrestler)">Yamato</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Open_the_Twin_Gate_Championship" title="Open the Twin Gate Championship">Open the Twin Gate Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_ROH_.282014.E2.80.932015.29">Return to ROH (2014–2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Return to ROH (2014–2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sydal made his return to Ring of Honor on September 27, 2014, losing to A.J. Styles at the <i><a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Honor_Wrestling" title="Ring of Honor Wrestling">Ring of Honor Wrestling</a></i> television tapings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In November, he was part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Survival_of_the_Fittest_(professional_wrestling)#2014" title="Survival of the Fittest (professional wrestling)">2014 Survival of the Fittest tournament</a>, won by <a href="/wiki/Adam_Cole" title="Adam Cole">Adam Cole</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> He unsuccessfully challenged Jay Lethal for the <a href="/wiki/ROH_World_Television_Championship" title="ROH World Television Championship">ROH World Television Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Final_Battle_2014" title="Final Battle 2014">Final Battle 2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> On August 21, 2015, Sydal defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Japan_Pro_Wrestling" title="New Japan Pro Wrestling">New Japan Pro Wrestling</a>'s <a href="/wiki/IWGP_Junior_Heavyweight_Championship" title="IWGP Junior Heavyweight Championship">IWGP Junior Heavyweight Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Yujiro_Kushida" title="Yujiro Kushida">Kushida</a> in a non-title match, after which Kushida accepted his challenge for a title match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Japan_Pro_Wrestling_.282015.E2.80.932016.29">New Japan Pro Wrestling (2015–2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: New Japan Pro Wrestling (2015–2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 23, 2015, Sydal made his debut for NJPW at <a href="/wiki/Destruction_in_Okayama_(2015)" title="Destruction in Okayama (2015)">Destruction in Okayaka</a>, teaming with <a href="/wiki/Hiroshi_Tanahashi" title="Hiroshi Tanahashi">Hiroshi Tanahashi</a> in a tag team match, where they defeated <a href="/wiki/Bad_Luck_Fale" title="Bad Luck Fale">Bad Luck Fale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tama_Tonga" title="Tama Tonga">Tama Tonga</a>. During the same event, the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IWGP_Junior_Heavyweight_Champion" title="IWGP Junior Heavyweight Champion">IWGP Junior Heavyweight Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Omega" title="Kenny Omega">Kenny Omega</a> nominated Sydal as the first challenger for his title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On October 12, at <a href="/wiki/King_of_Pro-Wrestling_(2015)" title="King of Pro-Wrestling (2015)">King of Pro-Wrestling</a>, Sydal unsuccessfully challenged Omega for the IWGP Junior Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> On October 24, Sydal and Ricochet entered the <a href="/wiki/Super_Junior_Tag_Tournament#2015" title="Super Junior Tag Tournament">2015 Super Jr. Tag Tournament</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Time_Splitters_(professional_wrestling)" title="Time Splitters (professional wrestling)">Time Splitters</a> (<a href="/wiki/Alex_Shelley" title="Alex Shelley">Alex Shelley</a> and Kushida) in their first round match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On November 1, Sydal and Ricochet defeated <a href="/wiki/The_Young_Bucks" title="The Young Bucks">The Young Bucks</a> (Matt and Nick Jackson) to advance to the finals of the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NJPW110115_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-NJPW110115-81">[81]</a></sup> On November 7, at <a href="/wiki/Power_Struggle_(2015)" title="Power Struggle (2015)">Power Struggle</a>, Sydal and Ricochet defeated <a href="/wiki/Roppongi_Vice" title="Roppongi Vice">Roppongi Vice</a> (<a href="/wiki/Trent_Barreta" title="Trent Barreta">Beretta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Romero" title="Rocky Romero">Rocky Romero</a>) in the finals to win the 2015 Super Jr. Tag Tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PowerStruggle2015_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-PowerStruggle2015-82">[82]</a></sup> On January 4, 2016, at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrestle_Kingdom_10_in_Tokyo_Dome" title="Wrestle Kingdom 10 in Tokyo Dome">Wrestle Kingdom 10 in Tokyo Dome</a>, Sydal and Ricochet took part in a four-way match for the <a href="/wiki/IWGP_Junior_Heavyweight_Tag_Team_Championship" title="IWGP Junior Heavyweight Tag Team Championship">IWGP Junior Heavyweight Tag Team Championship</a>, but were defeated by The Young Bucks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> On February 11 at <a href="/wiki/The_New_Beginning_in_Osaka_(2016)" title="The New Beginning in Osaka (2016)">The New Beginning in Osaka</a>, Sydal and Ricochet defeated The Young Bucks and <a href="/wiki/ReDRagon" title="ReDRagon">reDRagon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bobby_Fish" title="Bobby Fish">Bobby Fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyle_O%27Reilly" title="Kyle O'Reilly">Kyle O'Reilly</a>) in a three-way match to become the new IWGP Junior Heavyweight Tag Team Champions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BeginningOsaka2016_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-BeginningOsaka2016-84">[84]</a></sup> They lost the title to Roppongi Vice on April 10 at <a href="/wiki/Invasion_Attack_2016" title="Invasion Attack 2016">Invasion Attack 2016</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> before regaining the title on May 3 at <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_Dontaku_2016" title="Wrestling Dontaku 2016">Wrestling Dontaku 2016</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WrestlingDontaku2016_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-WrestlingDontaku2016-86">[86]</a></sup> Later in the month, Sydal entered the <a href="/wiki/Best_of_the_Super_Juniors#2016" title="Best of the Super Juniors">2016 Best of the Super Juniors</a>. He finished the tournament with five wins and two losses, tied with <a href="/wiki/Ryusuke_Taguchi" title="Ryusuke Taguchi">Ryusuke Taguchi</a>, but failed to advance to the finals due to losing to Taguchi in their head-to-head match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On June 19 at <a href="/wiki/Dominion_6.19_in_Osaka-jo_Hall" title="Dominion 6.19 in Osaka-jo Hall">Dominion 6.19 in Osaka-jo Hall</a>, Sydal and Ricochet lost the IWGP Junior Heavyweight Tag Team Championship to The Young Bucks in a four-way elimination match, also involving reDRagon and Roppongi Vice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 3, Sydal and Ricochet teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Satoshi_Kojima" title="Satoshi Kojima">Satoshi Kojima</a> to defeat Kenny Omega and The Young Bucks for the <a href="/wiki/NEVER_Openweight_6-Man_Tag_Team_Championship" title="NEVER Openweight 6-Man Tag Team Championship">NEVER Openweight 6-Man Tag Team Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KizunaRoad2016_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-KizunaRoad2016-89">[89]</a></sup> On July 20, Sydal, representing ROH, entered the <a href="/wiki/Super_J-Cup#2016" title="Super J-Cup">2016 Super J-Cup</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Kaientai_Dojo" title="Kaientai Dojo">Kaientai Dojo</a>'s Kaji Tomato in his first round match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> On August 21, Sydal defeated Will Ospreay in the second round of the tournament, before being eliminated in the semifinals by <a href="/wiki/Pro_Wrestling_Noah" title="Pro Wrestling Noah">Pro Wrestling Noah</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Yoshinobu_Kanemaru" title="Yoshinobu Kanemaru">Yoshinobu Kanemaru</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On September 25, Sydal, Ricochet and Kojima were stripped of the NEVER Openweight 6-Man Tag Team Championship due to Sydal failing to make a scheduled title defense at <a href="/wiki/Destruction_(2016)" title="Destruction (2016)">Destruction in Kobe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Sydal missed two shows over three days, officially due to "travel issues".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> It was later revealed that he had actually been arrested upon entering the country (<a href="#Arrest_in_Japan">see below</a>). He was replaced at Destruction in Kobe by David Finlay, who afterwards also took his spot as Ricochet's regular tag team partner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Sydal's profile has since been removed from NJPW official site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media">Other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Image Entertainment, Inc. released a DVD titled "Before They Were Stars: Matt Sydal: Bourne Is Born" on January 20, 2009, which features every match from <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_Society_X" title="Wrestling Society X">Wrestling Society X</a> Korklan participated in as well as various promos and a music video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DVD_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-DVD-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Both of Korklan's parents are school teachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varsallone_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-varsallone-97">[97]</a></sup> He has an older brother Mike, who wrestles under the name "Mike Sydal" in addition to one other brother who does not wrestle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> He attended <a href="/wiki/Parkway_West_High_School" title="Parkway West High School">Parkway West High School</a> in St. Louis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varsallone_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-varsallone-97">[97]</a></sup> In 2001, Korklan enrolled at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Missouri" title="University of Missouri">University of Missouri</a>, studying <a href="/wiki/Marketing" title="Marketing">marketing</a>, as he was unsure whether he could earn a living from wrestling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-smith-99">[99]</a></sup> He continued to wrestle, attending college three days a week, while wrestling mid-week and on weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-smith-99">[99]</a></sup> He graduated with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a> in 2005, and began working as a sales and marketing <a href="/wiki/Vice_president#Vice_presidents_in_business" title="Vice president">vice president</a> for a small mailbox company in St. Louis, although he continued to wrestle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-slam-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varsallone_97-2"><a href="#cite_note-varsallone-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-smith-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrest_in_Japan">Arrest in Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Sydal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Arrest in Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 23, 2016, Korklan was arrested at the <a href="/wiki/Kansai_International_Airport" title="Kansai International Airport">Kansai International Airport</a> under suspicion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marijuana" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a> smuggling. According to local authorities, Korklan had 2.12 grams of liquid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marijuana" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a> hidden with an electronic cigarette. Korklan was convicted in <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a> on October 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> On December 1, it was reported that Korklan had pled guilty to the charges and accepted three years of probation as his sentence. After a verdict the following week,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Korklan was released from prison and returned to the United States on December 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
